 flavor_fra.105.t:0 "Дама дивовижної краси та інтриги"
 flavor_fra.105.d:1 "One of the most prominent figures of French and English history, Eleanor of Aquitaine is a legendary figure weaved into the history of her domain. Famed for her wealth and power she came to control much of southern France during the 12th and 13th centuries. At the apogee of her influence, she married King Louis VII of France and participated in the Second Crusade as Queen Consort. Soon after their return, she requested a divorce which was eventually granted. At 30 years of age, she became engaged to her third cousin Henry, the duke of Normandy and count of Anjou, and upon their marriage ceremony, they were declared King and Queen of England, inaugurating the polity that would be later known as the Angevin Empire. Through expert statecraft and masterful manipulation of nobles and rulers alike, she carved her name in the books of history for the centuries to come, a shining example of a most capable queen."

 flavor_mng.30.d:0 "Careful selection of bureaucrats and administrators is a vital process for an empire with our size. This shared conduct will serve to cement our nation and promote unity, as well as the promotion of the meritocratic ideal that outlines the cornerstones of the founding of our dynasty. The examination system will therefore go on to play a significant role in tempering the power of hereditary aristocracy and military authority, and in the rise of a gentry class of scholar-bureaucrats."

 devshirme_system_reform:0 "Система девшірме"
 devshirme_system_reform_desc:0 "From the end of the 14th to the middle of the 17th century, the Ottoman dynasty acquired slaves for its household through the practice of devshirme. Carefully chosen Non-Muslim children, usually Christians from the rural Balkans between the ages of 12 and 14, were sent to live with Turkish families to learn Turkish and the rules of Islam before being brought to the imperial capital. Most joined the Janissaries, an infantry standing army trained under strict discipline, while those who displayed particular leadership and intellectual ability were enrolled directly into the sultan's household as pages, where they were educated and, if successful, could be promoted to the highest ranks of the Ottoman military-administrative elite. With their livelihood dependent upon the ruler, these slaves, known as kul, showed intense loyalty and were critical for the Ottoman dynasty's establishment of centralized control over the empire."

 ashigaru_reform:0 "Ashigaru Regiments"
 ashigaru_reform_desc:0 "The ubiquity of conflicts and wars in Japan during the Sengoku Jidai gave rise to a new class of warriors, the ashigaru. While peasants and technically not samurai, the easier accessibility to them in comparison to the samurai turned them into the backbone of any army. Armed with spears, bows and swords, their constant presence in battle made them into a class between the farmers and the samurai, being in some cases even considered as part of the lower strata of samurai. Hover, it was with the introduction of the tanegashima teppou, the Japanese adaption of the matchlock, that their presence truly shined. Its easier learning curve compared to the bow, combined with the superior numbers of the ashigaru compared to the samurai, made it so that ashigaru armed with matchlocks became the main part of any Japanese army."

 #Events 
 flavor_jap.62.t:0 "Rise of [4815.GetName]"
 flavor_jap.62.d:0 "The city of [4815.GetName], meaning Lion City and called Temasek in the past, rose as an important trading city for the different Malay and Javanese sea kingdoms and empires. It even served as the capital of the kingdom of Singapura, from which it later took the name. Situated at a crucial choke point of the trade flow between China and India, it has seen merchants and products from all places constantly come and go.\n\nHe who controls it, and the commerce that flows through it, will be able to be the one that controls the trade between the East and the West, benefiting greatly from both sides of it."
 flavor_jap.62.a:0 "Money makes the world go 'round."
 
 flavor_jap.63.t:0 "Період Едо"
 flavor_jap.63.d:0 "The Edo Period, historically starting in 1603 with the establishment of the Tokugawa Shogunate, marks a time of great stability, prosperity and economic growth for Japan. Finally free of internal struggles and constant civil wars, Japanese focus shifted instead towards the development not only of the economy but also of the arts and sciences. The increase in population saw also an increase in urbanization, which furthered such developments even more.\n\nThe period saw the creation and proliferation of new financial policies, new painting techniques like the ukiyo-e or new entertaining activities like the geisha or the kabuki and even new kinds of dishes like sushi or tempura. They all flourished during the Edo Period and became a staple of the Japanese culture recognized as such all over the world.\n\nWith this unprecedented period of stability, development and growth, our country is sure to be able to reach heights never before imagined."
 flavor_jap.63.a:0 "The struggles of the past are now behind us."
 
 flavor_jap.64.t:0 "Доля Мандата"
 flavor_jap.64.d:0 "Our country has always lived under the shadow of China. The big Dragon has always considered itself to be the center of the world and rightful ruler of all its territory by the Mandate of the Heaven itself. In the past we had been forced to accept these preposterous claims, but the Tiger has awakened, and it will obey the Dragon no more!\n\nIf there's a country that can claim to be instructed by Heaven itself to rule these lands it can be no other than our Divine Nation. We could take the throne of China for ourselves as it is, with all its associated bureaucracy, or let it die under the weight of a clearly superior and truly divinely authorized rule."
 flavor_jap.64.a:0 "It's mine and mine alone!"
 flavor_jap.64.b:0 "These petty declarations are beneath us..."
 
 flavor_jap.65.t:0 "Дім висхідного сонця"
 flavor_jap.65.d:0 "For far too long has our Divine Emperor been outshined by the military dictatorship of the Shogun. For far too long has His Divine Blood been relegated to linger in the shadows. Fortunately for us, unlike His ancestor the Sun Goddess Amaterasu did when She secluded Herself inside the cave, depriving the world of light, He didn't resign himself to living unfruitfully imprisoned inside the Imperial Palace. Instead, He toiled continuously, using His influences to secure favors and support.\n\nWith time, He managed to secure enough support to be able to force the Shogun to abolish the shogunate and re-instate the Imperial Line as the effective ruler of Japan. With a Living Kami again at the forefront of the country, our nation will once again enjoy divine prosperity."
 flavor_jap.65.a:0 "We have waited for far too long!"
 
 flavor_jap.66.t:0 "Книга п'яти кілець"
 flavor_jap.66.d:0 "Our country has given rise to many warriors of renown, but none has gained as much persistent fame as the legendary Miyamoto Musashi. Being called the best duelist of the history of Japan, he won his first duel at the age of thirteen, and started travelling and participating in duels around the whole country, remaining undefeated.\n\nHis experiences are transmitted through his 'Book of Five Rings', in which he explains all his martial arts techniques, mentality and philosophy. In its pages there's invaluable knowledge in the way of becoming the perfect warrior, and our armies could benefit a lot from reading it."
 flavor_jap.66.a:0 "These teachings will improve our §Yland army§!."
 flavor_jap.66.b:0 "Discard them, focus on the §Msea§! instead!"
 
 flavor_jap.67.t:0 "Of Spice and Herbs"
 flavor_jap.67.d:0 "Advisors, scholars, poets and even politicians have all taken part on the latest grand debate that's shaking the nation. Unlike the usual grim matters of war or poverty that afflict and take up the desks of our hierarchy, lately the question on everyone's mind is: Spice or Herbs? Certainly both sides have strong arguments for their case. Spices definitely have the extra flavor to make our food and drink have that special taste and kick whilst the tea and other herbs dutifully possess their healing as well as calming properties which have been with our nation for centuries."
 flavor_jap.67.a:0 "I love me some spice ..."
 flavor_jap.67.b:0 "... but herbs is where it's at!"
 
 flavor_jap.68.t:0 "Перша гейша"
 flavor_jap.68.d:0 "A Geisha (or Geiko) is a person of arts, essentially a performing female artist. As coin poured into the treasuries of Japan, a growing part of it was funneled into culture and entertainment. The most common form of entertainment in the pleasure districts, performed by men and women alike, was dancing and singing accompanied by instruments and teenage dancing girls called odoriko. When these girls grew up they adopted different names to continue working, one of these names бувши 'geisha'.\n\nIn time, geisha became to be appreciated for their art with song, dances and the shamisen, and became specialized in these kinds of entertainment."
 flavor_jap.68.a:0 "Such refinement and sophistication!"
 
 flavor_jap.69.t:0 "Poetry and Songs of the Edo Period"
 flavor_jap.69.d:1 "The prosperity of the Edo period allowed for an equal development and maturity of culture and entertainment, and especially many forms of theater and music appeared. The differences between the noble samurai class and the common townsfolk gave rise to specific styles of music and theater, which defined and differentiated themselves the more the classes were set apart. A specific style of music and metric was created during this time, named kouta or kinsei kouta-cho, and it was so influential that it still persists in folk music to this day. It was a style of music for the shamisen, a banjo-like instrument, designed to accompany the singing of a poem or a story.\n\nPoetry also went through its own period of development, with traditional styles being revived and expanded, and new ones being created. It was very common to write poetry in collaboration with other people while alternating stanzas, and even ordinary citizens began participating in that. The starting stanza of the chain began to be perceived as a poem in itself, which with time gave rise to the haiku.\n\nOld pond;\nfrog leaps in;\nwater sound."
 flavor_jap.69.a:0 "What a display of beauty and intellect."
 
 flavor_jap.70.t:0 "Way of Chonindo"
 flavor_jap.70.d:1 "The changes in society after the turbulent times of the Sengoku Jidai are quite obvious. The previous constant struggles across all Japan have finally subsided, and now we enjoy a somewhat stable internal peace which allows a more relaxed life for the common people. As a result, they are flocking to the quickly growing cities, and thus our previously rural population is giving rise to the Chonin (townspeople), and with that their own way of life called Chonindo. Their aspiration towards the samurai class and their values of bushido, together with a keen interest in the development of arts and science have resulted in a distinct new mass culture, focused on a great quality of workmanship. Poetry, performances, puppet-theaters, paintings, and all other forms of art are seeing great expansions."
 flavor_jap.70.a:0 "What a time to be alive!"
 
 flavor_jap.71.t:0 "Great Fire of Meireki"
 flavor_jap.71.d:0 "Started by a priest who allegedly was attempting to burn a cursed kimono, the Great Fire of Meireki decimated [1028.GetName] and claimed over 100,000 lives. Due to the nature of the buildings in [1028.GetName], which are made of wood and paper, the fire that started in the Hongo District quickly spread throughout the city. Sadly, the fact that we chose to construct our buildings so close to one another played a significant part in the fast spread of the fiery destruction."
 flavor_jap.71.a:0 "What a tragedy."
 
 flavor_jap.72.t:0 "Kanda Matsuri Festivals in [Root.Capital.GetName]"
 flavor_jap.72.d:1 "After the turbulent times and constant war of the Sengoku Jidai, numerous festivals (matsuri) were established to celebrate peace once it was achieved. One of the most famous ones is the one celebrated in Kanda Myojin in Edo, a shrine popular both among the samurai and the common classes. The numerous floats, mikoshi, and performances that go along the procession really have turned the matsuri into widely acclaimed celebrations, and the focus of city life when they happen."
 flavor_jap.72.a:0 "A celebration of our proudest victories!"
 
 flavor_jap.73.t:0 "Onna-Musha in the Edo Period"
 flavor_jap.73.d:0 "Originally serving as female bushi, the Onna-musha were esteemed warriors in the early days of our Empire. They were members of the samurai class in feudal Japan and were trained in the use of weapons to protect their household, family, and honor in times of war. Over time, they distinguished themselves in the battlefield as able commanders, scoring impressive victories and cementing their names in the books of history.\n\nHowever, because of the influence of Edo neo-Confucianism, the status of the Onna-musha began diminishing significantly. The function of Onna-musha changed in addition to their husbands. Samurai were no longer concerned with battles and war, they were bureaucrats. Women, specifically daughters of most upper class households, were soon pawns to dreams of success and power. The roaring ideals of fearless devotion and selflessness were gradually replaced by quiet, passive, civil obedience. Despite this, many still wish to serve the nation's military forces as commanders and humbly request to be allowed to lay their lives in service of our country's noble cause. One notable example of the female bushi icons is Ohori Tsuruhime. She has courageously been to battle several times and her claim to divine inspiration coupled with fighting skills has led to her being compared with the likes of Joan of Arc. Her legacy will surely establish her as one of the most recognizable female warriors in Japanese history."
 flavor_jap.73.a:0 "Allow the onna-musha to continue operating."
 flavor_jap.73.b:0 "Their era has ended, they will serve as pawns of power and mandate bureaucracy!"

 flavor_spa.18.t:0 "Арагонські інфанти"
 flavor_spa.18.d:1 "Арагонські інфанти are the sons and daughters of king Fernando I of Арагон and his wife Leonor de Alburquerque, who established the Trastámara dynasty in that kingdom after the Compromise of Caspe in 1412. They are also cousins of the Castilian king Juan II and conspired since early in his reign to control him and seize power in Castile, with the support of a faction of relatives and allies among the Castilian nobility. However, they were opposed by another faction headed by the Royal Constable Álvaro de Luna, who became the main support of king Juan II for two decades.\n\nThe situation deteriorated from 1437 when a new civil war broke out between the faction headed by the Арагонські інфанти, and the one headed by Álvaro de Luna and the heir to the throne Enrique, which came to a resolution at the Battle of Olmedo in [GetYear]."

 flavor_spa.22.t:0 "The Spanish Dollar"
 flavor_spa.22.d:1 "The monetary system in Castile in the second half of the 15th century was in chaos. The maravedí, the main currency of account, had been continually devalued since the 13th century. In addition, there were different regional currencies in the Iberian kingdoms, which complicated the economics of the political unification initiated by the wedding of Isabella of Castile and Ferdinand of Арагон.\n\n For this reason, a monetary reform was initiated in [GetYear], establishing a new gold coin, the ducat, and a new silver coin, the real, for use in both kingdoms. Given the unexpectedly large influx of silver coming from the Americas in the following decades, the use of the 'real de a ocho', which soon became widely known as the 'Spanish dollar', skyrocketed. It is considered the first global currency, since it was accepted by merchants all over the world, from Africa to America and from Europe to Asia."
 flavor_spa.22.a:0 "Show me the Spanish Dollars!"
 flavor_spa.23.t:0 "San Lorenzo de El Escorial"
 flavor_spa.23.d:1 "[Root.Monarch.GetName], monarch of [Root.GetName], has many nicknames. But one of the most accurate is “the Bureaucrat King”. [Root.GetMSheHeCap] has decided to establish a fixed capital, putting an end to the ancient tradition of the Iberian kings to travel continuously. [Root.GetMSheHeCap] has chosen Madrid because of its central position, not бувши dependent of any great lord or the Church, and some would say because of its good water supply. In any case, [Root.Monarch.GetName] does not like the city itself, so [Root.GetMSheHe] also has decided to build a large monastery on its mountainous outskirts, dedicated to Saint Lawrence, which would also be [Root.GetMJOGO] habitual residence. [Root.GetMSheHeCap] has gathered a large library and relics of saints there, and has turned it into the nerve center of the administration, presiding over the daily meetings of the different councils that deal with government affairs. Finally, [Root.GetMSheHe] has also established the royal family pantheon there, where all the Kings and Queens of [Root.GetName] after [Root.Monarch.GetName] will be buried."
 flavor_spa.23.a:0 "A capital worthy of a global empire!"

In [GetYear], he is preparing to set sail with a fleet of five ships and approximately 270 men to find a new route to the Spice Islands in the East Indies. His goal is to discover the passage that would go on to allow his ships to sail through the southern tip of South America and enter the Pacific Ocean.\n\nMagellan's journey may be fraught with difficulties, including starvation and battles with indigenous peoples, but he plans to eventually reach the East Indies, and come back through the Cape of Good Hope. Magellan's achievement shall pave the way for future explorers and traders to navigate the globe and open up new opportunities for European colonization and trade in the Americas and Asia."

 #Reforms
 tercios_reform:0 "Tercios"
 tercios_reform_desc:0 "The Tercios, literary 'A Third', were the backbone of the Spanish armies in the Early Modern Age. While historically the Tercios were not only drafted from Spain, but also from Italy or Wallonia, the most valuable Tercios were drafted from Spanish provinces. Tercios were almost unbeatable for decades in the battlefields across Europe and the Mediterranean, and were key to the evolution of European warfare."
 system_of_councils_reform:0 "System of Councils"
 system_of_councils_reform_desc:0 "The System of Councils, also known as the Polysynodial System, was developed by the Hispanic Monarchy to organize the government of its different territories in the Early Modern Age. The central administration was entrusted to a group of collegiate bodies, the Councils, made up of nobles, clergymen and burghers, directly managed by university-trained lawyers, the 'letrados'. The different Councils were either thematic, with powers throughout the Spanish Empire, or territorial, with their competencies set over each of the different kingdoms."
